                        cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Advanced MoS2/Carbon Anode for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jingjing; Luo, Chao; Gao, Tao; Langrock, Alex; Mignerey, Alice C.; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 is a promising anode for high-performance sodium-ion batteries due to high specific capacity, abundance, and low cost.  However, poor cycling stability, low rate capability and unclear electrochem. reaction mechanism are the main challenges for MoS2 anode in Na-ion batteries.  In this study, molybdenum disulfide/carbon (MoS2/C) nanospheres are fabricated and used for Na-ion battery anodes.  MoS2/C nanospheres deliver a reversible capacity of 520 mA-h/g at 0.1C and maintain capacity 400 mA-h/g for 300 cycles at a high c.d. of 1C, demonstrating the best cycling performance of MoS2 for Na-ion batteries to date.  The high capacity is attributed to the short ion and electron diffusion pathway, which enables fast charge transfer and low concn. polarization.  The stable cycling performance and high coulombic efficiency (∼100%) of MoS2/C nanospheres are ascribed to (a) highly reversible conversion reaction of MoS2 during sodiation/desodiation as evidenced by ex-situ x-ray diffraction and (b) the formation of a stable solid electrolyte interface layer in fluoroethylene carbonate based electrolyte as demonstrated by FTIR spectroscopy measurements.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqcL7gViWJlhrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh4UwadnYJVPQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhtlOitbg%253D&amp;md5=6ec4e5e6db41f69f19d690e591e04ffa</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201402563"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries and Sodium-Ion Pseudocapacitors Based on MoS2/Graphene Composites</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Yun-Xiao; Chou, Shu-Lei; Wexler, David; Liu, Hua-Kun; Dou, Shi-Xue</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion energy storage, including sodium-ion batteries and electrochem. capacitive storage, is considered as a promising alternative to lithium-ion energy storage.  It is an intriguing prospect, esp. for large-scale applications, owing to its low cost and abundance.  MoS2 sodiation/desodiation with Na ions is based on the conversion reaction, which is not only able to deliver higher capacity than the intercalation reaction, but can also be applied in capacitive storage owing to its typically sloping charge/discharge curves.  Here, sodium-ion batteries and sodium-ion pseudocapacitors based on a graphene composite (MoS2/graphene) were constructed.  The enlarged d-spacing, a contribution of the graphene matrix, and the unique properties of the MoS2/graphene substantially optimize Na storage behavior, by accommodating large vol. changes and facilitating fast ion diffusion.  MoS2/graphene exhibits a stable capacity of ∼350 mA-h/g over 200 cycles at 0.25C in half cells, and delivers a capacitance of 50 F/g over 2000 cycles at 1.5C in pseudocapacitors with a wide voltage window of 0.1-2.5 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqzTyHZli02abVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh4UwadnYJVPQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtV2ju73N&amp;md5=cd1ad639fc6ba622b13a18335a7c1125</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/chem.201400128"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical MoS2 Shells Supported on Carbon Spheres for Highly Reversible Lithium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Lei; Lou, Xiong Wen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry - A European Journal</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchical MoS2 shells supported on C spheres (denoted as C@MoS2) have been synthesized through a 1-step hydrothermal method.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Thin MoS2 Nanoflakes Encapsulated in Carbon Nanofibers as High-Performance Anodes for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Chenyang; Kong, Junhua; Yao, Xiayin; Tang, Xiaosheng; Dong, Yuliang; Phua, Si Lei; Lu, Xuehong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Highly flexible MoS2-based Li-ion battery anodes composed of disordered thin MoS2 nanoflakes encapsulated in amorphous C nanofibrous mats were fabricated for the 1st time through hydrothermal synthesis of graphene-like MoS2, followed by electrospinning and carbonization.  X-ray diffraction as well as scanning and transmission electron microscopic studies show that the as-synthesized MoS2 nanoflakes have a thickness of ∼5 nm with an expanded interlayer spacing, and their structure and morphol. are well-retained after the electrospinning and carbonization.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical nanotubes constructed from interlayer-expanded MoSe2 nanosheets as a highly durable electrode for sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Junjun; Wu, Meihui; Liu, Tong; Kang, Wenpei; Xu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">47</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">24859-24866</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as a promising energy storage device, but suffer from poor cycling performance.  Here, hierarchical MoSe2 nanotubes were synthesized for the 1st time and demonstrated as a highly durable electrode material of SIBs.  The hierarchical nanotubes consist of few-layered MoSe2 nanosheets with an expanded (002) interlayer spacing of 1.00 nm (54.8% expansion).  The growth of hierarchical nanotubes is a result of oriented attachment and Ostwald ripening effects.  As a robust Na host material, the MoSe2 nanotubes featuring hierarchical organization, hollow interiors, and interlayer expansion are beneficial for (1) lowering diffusion energy barriers and facilitating fast Na+ insertion/extn. reaction kinetics, (2) accommodating vol. changes upon sodiation/desodiation, (3) preserving structural and morphol. stability, and (4) improving electronic cond. by in situ C modification.  By controlling the cut-off voltage of 0.5-3.0 V with an intercalation mechanism, the MoSe2 nanotube electrode shows highly stable cycling performance and delivers a reversible discharge capacity of 228 mAh/g after 1500 cycles at a high c.d. of 1000 mA/g.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2 Nanoflowers with Expanded Interlayers as High-Performance Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Wang, Lixiu; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Cheng, Fangyi; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 nanoflowers with expanded interlayer spacing of the (002) plane were synthesized and used as high-performance anode in Na-ion batteries.  By controlling the cut-off voltage to the range of 0.4-3 V, an intercalation mechanism rather than a conversion reaction is taking place.  The MoS2 nanoflower electrode shows high discharge capacities of 350 mAh g-1 at 0.05 A g-1, 300 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1, and 195 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1.  An initial capacity increase with cycling is caused by peeling off MoS2 layers, which produces more active sites for Na+ storage.  The stripping of MoS2 layers occurring in charge/discharge cycling contributes to the enhanced kinetics and low energy barrier for the intercalation of Na+ ions.  The electrochem. reaction is mainly controlled by the capacitive process, which facilitates the high-rate capability.  Therefore, MoS2 nanoflowers with expanded interlayers hold promise for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp0lywDrXEibbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljintAxsCKvww"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFShtL3P&amp;md5=218e207e71a96b8802293b3796174e5a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201402428"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Choi, S.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D MoS2-Graphene Microspheres Consisting of Multiple Nanospheres with Superior Sodium Ion Storage Properties</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Choi, Seung Ho; Ko, You Na; Lee, Jung-Kul; Kang, Yun Chan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A novel anode material for sodium-ion batteries consisting of 3D graphene microspheres divided into several tens of uniform nanospheres coated with few-layered MoS2 by a one-pot spray pyrolysis process is prepd.  The first discharge/charge capacities of the composite microspheres are 797 and 573 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 0.2 A g-1.  The 600th discharge capacity of the composite microspheres at a c.d. of 1.5 A g-1 is 322 mA h g-1.  The Coulombic efficiency during the 600 cycles is as high as 99.98%.  The outstanding Na ion storage properties of the 3D MoS2-graphene composite microspheres may be attributed to the reduced stacking of the MoS2 layers and to the 3D structure of the porous graphene microspheres.  The reduced stacking of the MoS2 layers relaxes the strain and lowers the barrier for Na+ insertion.  The empty nanospheres of the graphene offer voids for vol. expansion and pathways for fast electron transfer during repeated cycling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5MXJGPkuEhLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljintAxsCKvww"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXkvVSitbk%253D&amp;md5=18c752a0885c5236fc4aefe504f5d301</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.201404078"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>/Graphene Composite Anodes with Enhanced Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Role of the Two-Dimensional Heterointerface</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2/Graphene Composite Anodes with Enhanced Performance for Sodium-Ion Batteries: The Role of the Two-Dimensional Heterointerface</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xie, Xiuqiang; Ao, Zhimin; Su, Dawei; Zhang, Jinqiang; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1393-1403</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AFMDC6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1616-301X</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphene has been widely used as conformal nanobuilding blocks to improve the electrochem. performance of layered metal sulfides (MoS2, WS2, SnS, and SnS2) as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  However, it still lacks in-depth understanding of the synergistic effect between these layered sulfides and graphene, which contributes to the enhanced electroactivity for sodium-ion batteries.  Here, MoS2/reduced graphene oxide (RGO) nanocomposites with intimate two-dimensional heterointerfaces are prepd. by a facile one-pot hydrothermal method.  The heterointerfacial area can be effectively tuned by changing the ratio of MoS2 to RGO.  When used as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries, the synergistic effect contributing to the enhanced reversible capacity of MoS2/RGO nanocomposites is closely related with the heterointerfacial area.  The computational results demonstrate that Na prefers to be adsorbed on MoS2 in the MoS2/RGO heterostructure rather than intercalate into the MoS2/RGO heterointerface.  Interestingly, the MoS2/RGO heterointerfaces can significantly increase the electronic cond. of MoS2, store more Na ions, while maintaining the high diffusion mobility of Na atoms on MoS2 surface and high electron transfer efficiency from Na to MoS2.  It is expected that the efforts to establish the correlation between the two-dimensional heterointerface and the electrochem. sodium-ion storage performance offer fundamental understanding for the rational design of layered metal sulfides/graphene composites as high-performance electrode materials for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpB50PmkRDAvrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljintAxsCKvww"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVansbY%253D&amp;md5=3d82ce10422e6d348a48b628852d1b2b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201308354"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">van Aken, P.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Single-Layered Ultrasmall Nanoplates of MoS2 Embedded in Carbon Nanofibers with Excellent Electrochemical Performance for Lithium and Sodium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Changbao; Mu, Xiaoke; van Aken, Peter A.; Yu, Yan; Maier, Joachim</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The prepn. and electrochem. storage behavior of MoS2 nanodots-more precisely single-layered ultrasmall nanoplates-embedded in C nanowires was studied.  The prepn. is achieved by an electrospinning process that can be easily scaled up.  The rate performance and cycling stability of both Li and Na storage are outstanding.  The storage behavior is, also, highly exciting from a fundamental point of view, as the differences between the usual storage modes-insertion, conversion, interfacial storage-are beneficially blurred.  The restriction to ultrasmall reaction domains allows for an almost diffusion-less and nucleation-free conversion, thereby resulting in a high capacity and a remarkable cycling performance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpG0S-uNUBpErVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liLIGzX2WIBMg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVOksbs%253D&amp;md5=254287c1e0aaa7c0c4e4780af2097bf6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2016.11.170"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Chemical Vapor Deposited MoS<sub>2</sub>/Electrospun Carbon Nanofiber Composite as Anode Material for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Chemical vapor deposited MoS2/electrospun carbon nanofiber composite as anode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Chen; Li, Guoqing; Lu, Yao; Zhu, Jiadeng; Jiang, Mengjin; Hu, Yi; Cao, Linyou; Zhang, Xiangwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">222</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1751-1760</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to its high theor. capacity and unique layered structure, MoS2 has attracted attention as a Na-ion battery anode material.  However, the electrochem. performance of MoS2 based anodes is hindered by their low intrinsic cond. and large vol. change during cycling.  Nano-sized MoS2 sheets were synthesized using a scalable CVD method on the surface of electrospun C nanofibers (CNFs).  The morphol. of the resultant MoS2@CNFs was studied by SEM, TEM and x-ray diffraction, while their electrochem. performance was studied using cyclic voltammetry and galvanostatic charge-discharge.  A strong interconnection between MoS2 nanosheets and CNFs is formed and the conductive network of CNFs is beneficial for the Na ion kinetics.  When studied as an anode for Na-ion batteries, a high reversible capacity of 380 mA h g-1 was obtained after 50 cycles with good cycling stability.  In particular, MoS2@CNFs can deliver a capacity of 198 mA h g-1 under a high c.d. of 1 A g-1 after 500 cycles, indicating their great potential as anode material for long-life Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpINaOxNvKXNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liLIGzX2WIBMg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhvF2gu7vF&amp;md5=1125a03e3dca583bd705f6da2fb4f1c6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1039/C7TA00030H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">2D MoS<sub>2</sub>/Polyaniline Heterostructures with Enlarged Interlayer Spacing for Superior Lithium and Sodium Storage</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">2D MoS2/polyaniline heterostructures with enlarged interlayer spacing for superior lithium and sodium storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Haiyan; Jiang, Hao; Hu, Yanjie; Li, Neng; Zhao, Xiujian; Li, Chunzhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5383-5389</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The exploitation of high-capacity and long-life MoS2-based materials is highly important for developing lithium ion batteries (LIBs) and sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  Herein, we demonstrate the confined synthesis of 2D MoS2/polyaniline (MoS2/PANI) nanosheet heterostructures with well-defined interfaces, in which the interlayer distance of MoS2 is greatly enlarged from 0.62 nm to 1.08 nm.  The introduction of such a big interlayer distance for efficient Li+/Na+ storage has never been demonstrated before.  The unique MoS2/PANI nanosheets can address well the key challenges of traditional MoS2 anode materials related to low cond. particularly in the vertical direction, easy restacking/aggregation, large volumetric change and sluggish Li+/Na+ diffusion kinetics in the interlamination.  Consequently, they deliver a high reversible capacity, superior rate capability and long cycle life for both LIBs and SIBs.  A state-of-the-art ab initio mol. dynamics (AIMD) simulation also reveals that MoS2/PANI nanosheets with enlarged interlayer spacing possess a remarkably improved Li+/Na+ diffusion mobility compared to pristine MoS2 nanosheets.  The present material design concept opens new directions for finding efficient LIBs/SIBs anodes with high capacity, rate capability and stability.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGquzhp71mABWrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liLIGzX2WIBMg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXitFCqt7c%253D&amp;md5=6ce25692e1055c75cff1efcbd438be75</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref25'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201600289"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xue, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoS<sub>2</sub>-Based Nanocomposites for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2-Based Nanocomposites for Electrochemical Energy Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang Tianyi; Xue Huaiguo; Chen Shuangqiang; Pang Huan; Yu Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Typical layered transition-metal chalcogenide materials, in particular layered molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) nanocomposites, have attracted increasing attention in recent years due to their excellent chemical and physical properties in various research fieldsHere, a general overview of synthetic MoS2 based nanocomposites via different preparation approaches and their applications in energy storage devices (Li-ion battery, Na-ion battery, and supercapacitor) is presented.  The relationship between morphologies and the electrochemical performances of MoS2-based nanocomposites in the three typical and promising rechargeable systems is also discussed.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene-Like MoS2/Graphene Composites: Cationic Surfactant-Assisted Hydrothermal Synthesis and Electrochemical Reversible Storage of Lithium</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Guochuang; Chen, Tao; Chen, Weixiang; Wang, Zhen; Chang, Kun; Ma, Lin; Huang, Feihe; Chen, Dongyun; Lee, Jim Yang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">21</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3693-3703</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1613-6810</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A cationic surfactant-assisted hydrothermal route is developed for the facile synthesis of graphene-like MoS2/graphene (GL-MoS2/G) composites based on the hydrothermal redn. of Na2MoO4 and graphene oxide sheets with L-cysteine in the presence of cetyltrimethylammonium bromide (CTAB), following by annealing in N2 atmosphere.  The GL-MoS2/G composites are characterized by X-ray diffraction, electron microscopy, high-resoln. transmission electron microscopy, and Raman spectroscopy.  The effects of CTAB concn. on the microstructures and electrochem. performances of the composites for reversible Li+ storage are investigated.  It is found that the layer no. of MoS2 sheets decreases with increasing CTAB concn.  The GL-MoS2 sheets in the composites are few-layer in the case of 0.01∼0.03 mol L-1 CTAB of hydrothermal soln. and single-layer in the case of 0.05 mol L-1 CTAB.  The GL-MoS2/G composites prepd. with 0.01-0.02 mol·L-1 of CTAB soln. exhibit a higher reversible capacity of 940-1020 mAh g-1, a greater cycle stability, and a higher rate capability than other samples.  The exceptional electrochem. performance of GL-MoS2/G composites for reversible Li+ storage could be attributed to an effective integration of GL-MoS2 sheets and graphene that maximizes the synergistic interaction between them.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoO05Nhzci-HLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liLIGzX2WIBMg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXpsV2rtbg%253D&amp;md5=003c32147cd1761af9fc939408fdc7bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1039/c3cc38598a"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bindumadhavan, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Srivastava, S.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical NiCo2O4 nanosheets on carbon nanofiber films for high energy density and long-life Li-O2 batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Guoxue; Zhang, Lei; Wang, Suqing; Ding, Liang-Xin; Wang, Haihui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Designing O cathodes with both high energy d. and excellent cycling stability is a great challenge in the development of Li-O (Li-O2) batteries for energy storage systems.  Herein, the authors design a novel structure of hierarchical NiCo2O4 nanosheets on porous C nanofiber films (denoted as NiCo2O4@CNFs) as an O cathode for Li-O batteries.  The NiCo2O4@CNFs cathode delivers a high specific discharge capacity of 4179 mA-h g-1, a high energy d. of 2110 W h kg-1 and superior cycling stability over 350 cycles.  The excellent electrochem. performance of the NiCo2O4@CNFs cathode can be attributed to the rational design and engineering of catalysts and porous conductive electrodes.  The NiCo2O4@CNFs electrode is a promising candidate for high energy d. and long-life Li-O2 batteries.  Addnl., the rational design of the hierarchical catalyst constructed low-dimensional nanostructure and the lightwt. porous C nanofiber electrode can be also used for other metal-O batteries, such as Zn-O (Zn-O2) batteries, Al-O (Al-O2) batteries, and Na-O (Na-O2) batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpEmO75_Ob9CrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh21LbqWipXsw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtVCltbvP&amp;md5=f40f87963c032c79119d1c2c629e37f0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201400910"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tong, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible Energy-Storage Devices: Design Consideration and Recent Progress</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible Energy-Storage Devices: Design Consideration and Recent Progress</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xianfu; Lu, Xihong; Liu, Bin; Chen, Di; Tong, Yexiang; Shen, Guozhen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Flexible energy storage devices are attracting increasing attention as they show unique promising advantages, such as flexibility, shape diversity, light wt.; these properties enable applications in portable, flexible, and even wearable electronic devices, including soft electronic products, roll-up displays, and wearable devices.  Consequently, considerable effort has been made in recent years to fulfill the requirements of future flexible energy storage devices, and much progress has been witnessed.  This paper describes the most recent advances in flexible energy storage devices, including flexible lithium-ion batteries and flexible supercapacitors.  The latest successful examples in flexible lithium-ion batteries and their technol. innovations and challenges are reviewed first.  This is followed by a detailed overview of the recent progress in flexible supercapacitors based on carbon materials and a no. of composites and flexible micro-supercapacitors.  Some of the latest achievements regarding interesting integrated energy storage systems are also reviewed.  Further research direction is also proposed to surpass existing technol. bottle-necks and realize idealized flexible energy storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp5NXiYiQAAgLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh21LbqWipXsw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpsValtLc%253D&amp;md5=64a6729ce362adf7c1e49db7967f91f3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1126/science.1151831"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nishide, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oyaizu, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Toward Flexible Batteries</span>. <i>Science</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2008</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>319</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">737</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">738</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Uniform growth of MoS2 nanosheets on carbon nanofibers with enhanced electrochemical utilization for Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jian-Gan; Zhou, Rui; Jin, Dandan; Xie, Keyu; Wei, Bingqing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">231</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">396-402</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile route for the uniform growth of MoS2 nanosheets on C nanofibers (CNFs) via a simple hydrothermal method is reported.  The CNF network provides a porous and three-dimensional scaffold for the deposition of ultrathin MoS2 nanosheets.  Benefiting from the highly conductive and porous CNFs as well as the nanostructured MoS2, the coaxial MoS2@CNF nanocomposites(*), when served as a binder-free and flexible anode for Li-ion batteries, could generate a synergistic effect to gain a high electrochem. use of MoS2.  As a result, the nanocomposites exhibit a high reversible capacity of 846 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, excellent high-rate capability (455 mAh g-1 even at 2 A g-1), and good cycling retention with only 7.4% capacity degrdn. after 100 cycles.  The superior Li-ion storage properties enable the nanocomposites to hold great potential application in high-performance Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpoWW2Oa6NaDbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhC_GBJJ0F5YQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXjtlKjtL0%253D&amp;md5=0ba47aa1de112e2da270728a2ef04d6a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit36" data-doi="10.1039/C5NR02711J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Miao, Y.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospun porous carbon nanofiber@MoS2 core/sheath fiber membranes as highly flexible and binder-free anodes for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Miao, Yue-E.; Huang, Yunpeng; Zhang, Longsheng; Fan, Wei; Lai, Feili; Liu, Tianxi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">25</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11093-11101</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Self-standing membranes of porous carbon nanofiber (PCNF)@MoS2 core/sheath fibers have been facilely obtained through a combination of electrospinning, high-temp. carbonization and the solvothermal reaction.  PCNF fibers with porous channels are used as building blocks for the construction of hierarchical PCNF@MoS2 composites where thin MoS2 nanosheets are uniformly distributed on the PCNF surface.  Thus, a three-dimensional open structure is formed, which provides a highly conductive pathway for rapid charge-transfer reactions, as well as greatly improving the surface active sites of MoS2 for fast lithiation/delithiation of Li+ ions.  The highly flexible PCNF@MoS2 composite membrane electrode exhibits synergistically improved electrochem. performance with a high specific capacity of 954 mA h g-1 upon the initial discharge, a high rate capability of 475 mA h g-1 even at a high c.d. of 1 A g-1, and good cycling stability with almost 100% retention after 50 cycles, indicating its potential application as a binder-free anode for high-performance lithium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpMPD2zFIzF7LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhC_GBJJ0F5YQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXosFKktrc%253D&amp;md5=d2147a0357cec5371ea138b0d9053a33</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref37"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">37</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit37" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201502161"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xie, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Makaryan, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Van Aken, K.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2/Graphene Composite Paper for Sodium-Ion Battery Electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">David, Lamuel; Bhandavat, Romil; Singh, Gurpreet</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We study the synthesis and electrochem. and mech. performance of layered free-standing papers composed of acid-exfoliated few-layer molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) and reduced graphene oxide (rGO) flakes for use as a self-standing flexible electrode in sodium-ion batteries.  Synthesis was achieved through vacuum filtration of homogeneous dispersions consisting of varying wt. percent of acid-treated MoS2 flakes in GO in DI water, followed by thermal redn. at elevated temps.  The electrochem. performance of the crumpled composite paper (at 4 mg.cm-2) was evaluated as counter electrode against pure Na foil in a half-cell configuration.  The electrode showed good Na cycling ability with a stable charge capacity of ∼230 mAh.g-1 with respect to total wt. of the electrode with Coulombic efficiency reaching ∼99%.  In addn., static uniaxial tensile tests performed on crumpled composite papers showed high av. strain to failure reaching ∼2%.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqX-na1eCQtCLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhC_GBJJ0F5YQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Synthesis of MoS2 and MoSe2 Films with Vertically Aligned Layers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kong, Desheng; Wang, Haotian; Cha, Judy J.; Pasta, Mauro; Koski, Kristie J.; Yao, Jie; Cui, Yi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1341-1347</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Layered materials consist of mol. layers stacked together by weak interlayer interactions.  They often crystallize to form atomically smooth thin films, nanotubes, and platelet or fullerene-like nanoparticles due to the anisotropic bonding.  Structures that predominately expose edges of the layers exhibit high surface energy and are often considered unstable.  The authors present a synthesis process to grow MoS2 and MoSe2 thin films with vertically aligned layers, thereby maximally exposing the edges on the film surface.  Such edge-terminated films are metastable structures of MoS2 and MoSe2, which may find applications in diverse catalytic reactions.  The authors confirmed their catalytic activity in a hydrogen evolution reaction (HER), in which the exchange c.d. correlates directly with the d. of the exposed edge sites.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGquOt3swEujfbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhC_GBJJ0F5YQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXitFajsLY%253D&amp;md5=12750e01fd7cb5c14b79f2c6168d02b0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2018.03.002"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cai, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Song, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Neale, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H. E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sui, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">MoSe<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets Perpendicularly Grown on Graphene with Mo-C Bonding for Sodium-Ion Capacitors</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>47</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">224</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">234</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2018.03.002</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D47%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D224-234%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DX.%2BZhao%26author%3DW.%2BCai%26author%3DY.%2BYang%26author%3DX.%2BSong%26author%3DZ.%2BNeale%26author%3DH.%2BE.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BSui%26author%3DG.%2BCao%26title%3DMoSe2%2BNanosheets%2BPerpendicularly%2BGrown%2Bon%2BGraphene%2Bwith%2BMo-C%2BBonding%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BCapacitors%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2018.03.002&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b05825&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2018.03.002&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoSe2 nanosheets perpendicularly grown on graphene with Mo-C bonding for sodium-ion capacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Xu; Cai, Wei; Yang, Ying; Song, Xuedan; Neale, Zachary; Wang, Hong-En; Sui, Jiehe; Cao, Guozhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">47</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">224-234</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional (2D) MoSe2/graphene nanocomposites show great potential as anode materials for sodium ion batteries (SIBs).  In this work, we report the controlled growth of oriented, interlayer-expanded MoSe2 nanosheets on graphene with Mo-C bonding via a surfactant-directed hydrothermal reaction.  The resulting 2D nanocomposite with strong electronic coupling facilitates both electron and Na-ion transfer across the interface and reversible insertion/extn. of Na-ion, enabling fast pseudocapacitive Na-ion storage with reduced voltage hysteresis and excellent durability over 1500 cycles.  D. Functional Theory (DFT) calcn. demonstrated MoSe2/graphene established a charge accumulation at the interface and promoted sodium-ion transport through the interface.  Such outstanding Na-ion storage capability propels their potential application in sodium-ion capacitors (SICs).  As a proof-of-concept, a model hybrid SIC was demonstrated by assembling with MoSe2/graphene composite as anode and activated carbon as cathode, delivering an impressive energy d. of 82 W h kg-1 and power output of 10,752 W kg-1 within a voltage window of 0.5-3 V.  The SIC also delivered a superior rate capability (66% capacitance retention after increasing the c.d. from 0.1 to 25.6 A g-1) and cyclability (81% capacitance retention over 5000 cycles at 5 A g-1), which shows promise for bridging the performance gap between conventional batteries and supercapacitors.  The proposed strategy based on hierarchical hybridization combined with chem. bonding and interlayer engineering may hold great promise for developing advanced electrode materials for next-generation clean energy systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo33opTzwi6vbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3taMd0-7QAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXktlynu78%253D&amp;md5=ff2e7fc742471e5286007c2209007324</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref42"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">42</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit42" data-doi="10.1021/nn200659w"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, W.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">L-Cysteine-Assisted Synthesis of Layered MoS<sub>2</sub>/Graphene Composites with Excellent Electrochemical Performances for Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">4720</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">4728</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">L-Cysteine-Assisted Synthesis of Layered MoS2/Graphene Composites with Excellent Electrochemical Performances for Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chang, Kun; Chen, Weixiang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4720-4728</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A facile process was developed to synthesize layered MoS2/graphene (MoS2/G) composites by an L-cysteine-assisted soln.-phase method, in which sodium molybdate, as-prepd. graphene oxide (GO), and L-cysteine were used as starting materials.  As-prepd. MoS2/G was then fabricated into layered MoS2/G composites after annealing in a H2/N2 atmosphere at 800° for 2 h.  The samples were systematically studied by x-ray diffraction, field emission SEM, energy dispersive X-ray spectroscopy, and high-resoln. TEM.  Electrochem. performances were evaluated in two-electrode cells vs. metallic lithium.  The obtained MoS2/G composites show three-dimensional architecture and excellent electrochem. performances as anode materials for Li-ion batteries.  The MoS2/G composite with a Mo:C molar ratio of 1:2 exhibits the highest specific capacity of ∼1100 mAh/g at a current of 100 mA/g, as well as excellent cycling stability and high-rate capability.  The superior electrochem. performances of MoS2/G composites as Li-ion battery anodes are attributed to their robust composite structure and the synergistic effects between layered MoS2 and graphene.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqCZ2OkL_eUGbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3taMd0-7QAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3MXmtlyms7c%253D&amp;md5=1ab1063ee9a071ae41ed3a39f457ff97</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.03.027"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospinning with Partially Carbonization in Air: Highly Porous Carbon Nanofibers Optimized for High-Performance Flexible Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nano Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>13</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">693</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">701</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.03.027</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D13%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D693-701%26journal%3DNano%2BEnergy%26author%3DW.%2BLi%26author%3DM.%2BLi%26author%3DM.%2BWang%26author%3DL.%2BZeng%26author%3DY.%2BYu%26title%3DElectrospinning%2Bwith%2BPartially%2BCarbonization%2Bin%2BAir%253A%2BHighly%2BPorous%2BCarbon%2BNanofibers%2BOptimized%2Bfor%2BHigh-Performance%2BFlexible%2BLithium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.nanoen.2015.03.027&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.8b05825&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.nanoen.2015.03.027&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospinning with partially carbonization in air: Highly porous carbon nanofibers optimized for high-performance flexible lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Weihan; Li, Minsi; Wang, Min; Zeng, Linchao; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">693-701</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Self-supported and flexible highly porous carbon nanofibers (HPCNFs) were prepd. by electrospinning method combined with a post-two-step carbonization process.  By introduction of air into the Ar flow during carbonization, carbon nanofibers were partially burnt off and a large no. of micro/mesopores were created.  As effective lithium storage units, the porous structure plays an important role in enhancing the electrochem. performances.  The HPCNFs delivers a reversible capacity as high as 1780 mAh g-1 after 40 cycles at 50 mA g-1 and ultralong cycle life (1550 mAh g-1 after 600 cycles at 500 mA g-1).  Even cycled at 25 A g-1, it still displays a very high capacity of 200 mAh g-1.  The outstanding electrochem. and mech. properties of HPCNFs are attributed to the novel structure: pores provide good access of the electrolyte to the electrode surface and facilitate fast charge transfer across the electrode/electrolyte interface. 3D interconnected networks decrease the contact resistance and improve elec. cond. of the overall electrode, which enhance electron transport rate.  Therefore, this novel carbon material holds great promise for potential applications in energy-related technol. and flexible electrodes for next generation LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpNd91PVUFXXbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3taMd0-7QAw"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D Porous N-Doped Graphene Frameworks Made of Interconnected Nanocages for Ultrahigh-Rate and Long-Life Li-O2 Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Changtai; Yu, Chang; Liu, Shaohong; Yang, Juan; Fan, Xiaoming; Huang, Huawei; Qiu, Jieshan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">25</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The inferior rate capability and poor cycle stability of the present Li-O2 batteries are still crit. obstacles for practice applications.  Configuring novel and integrated air electrode materials with unique structure and tunable chem. compns. is one of the efficient strategies to solve these bottleneck problems.  Herein, a novel strategy for synthesis of 3-dimensional porous N-doped graphene aerogels (NPGAs) with frameworks constructed by interconnected nanocages with the aid of polystyrene sphere@polydopamine is reported.  The interconnected nanocages as the basic building unit of graphene sheets are assembled inside the skeletons of 3-dimensional graphene aerogels, leading to the 3-dimensional NPGA with well-developed interconnected channels and the full exposure of electrochem. active sites.  Benefiting from such an unique structure, the as-made NPGA delivers a high specific capacity, an excellent rate capacity of 5978 mA-h g-1 at 3.2 A g-1, and long cycle stability, esp. at a large c.d. (54 cycles at 1 A g-1), indicative of boosted rate capability and cycle life as air electrodes for Li-O2 batteries.  More importantly, based on the total mass of C+Li2O2, a gravimetric energy d. of 2400 W h kg-1 for the NPGA-O2//Li cell is delivered at a power d. of 1300 W kg-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp_VKX1ezY-r7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj3taMd0-7QAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1yksrvL&amp;md5=9d298dc194a6716507ad8733878df3ec</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2017.08.030"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Norouzi

                        cas_cit46R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">46</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced sodium storage capability enabled by super wide-interlayer-spacing MoS2 integrated on carbon fibers</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Changtai; Yu, Chang; Zhang, Mengdi; Sun, Qian; Li, Shaofeng; Norouzi Banis, Mohammad; Han, Xiaotong; Dong, Qiang; Yang, Juan; Wang, Gang; Sun, Xueliang; Qiu, Jieshan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">41</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">66-74</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing advanced electrode materials for effective pseudocapacitive charge storage is one of effective strategies to enhance the rate capability and cycling stability of sodium ion storage devices.  Herein, we fabricate MoS2 nanoflowers with super wide interlayer spacing (nearly twice as large as that of the original MoS2) supported on carbon fibers (named as E-MoS2/carbon fibers) and demonstrate its superior electrochem. performances as flexible and binder-free anodes for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) and sodium-ion hybrid capacitors (SIHCs).  Grafting MoS2 nanoflowers onto the carbon fiber networks not only ensures the fast electron transfer, but also endows it with flexible feature.  The super wide interlayer spacing of MoS2 nanoflowers can not only decrease the ion diffusion pathways and resistance, but also increase their available and accessible active surface area, thus guaranteeing the rapid mass transport.  Also, it can accommodate the large internal strain during discharge/charge processes.  Benefiting from these combined structure merits, the E-MoS2/carbon fibers electrodes deliver an ultralong cycling stability up to 3000 cycles and the superior rate capacity of 104 mA h g-1 at 20 A g-1, which just takes ca. 18.7 s to fully charge/discharge.  When further employed as the anode for SIHCs, it delivers high energy and power densities due to the high pseudocapacitive charge storage of the super wide interlayer spacing E-MoS2/carbon fibers.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGom_c5ywhsXr7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljP1dO-H2YmpA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit48R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">48</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Carbon Nanofibers Decorated with Molybdenum Disulfide Nanosheets: Synergistic Lithium Storage and Enhanced Electrochemical Performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Fei; Xin, Sen; Liang, Hai-Wei; Song, Lu-Ting; Yu, Shu-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Traditional lithium-ion batteries that are based on layered Li intercalation electrode materials are limited by the intrinsically low theor. capacities of both electrodes and cannot meet the increasing demand for energy.  A facile route for the synthesis of a new type of composite nanofibers, namely carbon nanofibers decorated with molybdenum disulfide sheets (CNFs@MoS2), is now reported.  A synergistic effect was obsd. for the two-component anode, triggering new electrochem. processes for lithium storage, with a persistent oxidn. from Mo (or MoS2) to MoS3 in the repeated charge processes, leading to an ascending capacity upon cycling.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Pre-lithiation of onion-like carbon/MoS2 nano-urchin anodes for high-performance rechargeable lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Ye; Xing, Guozhong; Han, Zhao Jun; Shi, Yumeng; Wong, Jen It; Huang, Zhi Xiang; Ostrikov, Kostya; Yang, Hui Ying</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8884-8890</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hybrid urchin-like nanostructures composed of a spherical onion-like carbon (OLC) core and MoS2 nanoleaves were synthesized by a simple solvothermal method followed by thermal annealing treatment.  Compared to com. MoS2 powder, MoS2/OLC nanocomposites exhibit enhanced electrochem. performance as anode materials of lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) with a specific capacity of 853 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 50 mA g-1 after 60 cycles, and a moderate initial coulombic efficiency of 71.1%.  Furthermore, a simple pre-lithiation method based on direct contact of lithium foil with MoS2/OLC nano-urchins was used to achieve a very high coulombic efficiency of 97.6% in the first discharge/charge cycle, which is at least 26% higher compared to that of pristine MoS2/OLC nano-urchins.  This pre-lithiation method can be generalized to develop other carbon-metal sulfide nanohybrids for LIB anode materials.  These results may open up a new avenue for the development of the next-generation high-performance LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp3XaVKGFW2CrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljP1dO-H2YmpA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVelsrvJ&amp;md5=4befe7244741e95a776c015eca7eed9d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1038/srep09254"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qie, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flexible Membranes of MoS<sub>2</sub>/C Nanofibers by Electrospinning as Binder-Free Anodes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Sci.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible Membranes of MoS2/C Nanofibers by Electrospinning as Binder-Free Anodes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xiong, Xiaoqin; Luo, Wei; Hu, Xianluo; Chen, Chaoji; Qie, Long; Hou, Dongfang; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific Reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A flexible membrane consisting of MoS2/carbon nanofibers has been fabricated by a simple electrospinning method.  MoS2 nanosheets are uniformly encapsulated in the inter-connected carbon nanofibers with diams. of ∼150 nm.  When evaluated as a binder-free electrode for sodium-ion batteries, the as-obtained electrode demonstrates high performances, including high reversible capacity of 381.7 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 and superior rate capability (283.3, 246.5 and 186.3 mA h g-1 at 0.5, 1 and 2 A g-1, resp.).                         cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Encapsulation of Sn@carbon Nanoparticles in Bamboo-like Hollow Carbon Nanofibers as an Anode Material in Lithium-Based Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yu, Yan; Gu, Lin; Wang, Chunlei; Dhanabalan, Abirami; van Aken, Peter A.; Maier, Joachim</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2009</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">48</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">35</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6485-6489, S6485/1-S6485/3</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A Sn/C composite structure, namely Sn@carbon encapsulated in bamboo-like hollow carbon nanofibers, was fabricated by pyrolysis of TBT (core)/PAN (sheath) nanofibers through coaxial electrospinning.  As anode material for lithium batteries (LIBs) this composite displays a high reversible capacity of 737 mA-h/g after 200 cycles at 0.5 C.  It also exhibits a reversible discharge capacity as high as 480 mA-h/g when cycled at 5 C.  The particular Sn@carbon encapsulated in hollow carbon nanofibers structure has a high Sn content (close to 70% Sn and 30% carbon) and provides appropriate void vol. to respond to large vol. changes and to prevent pulverization of the Sn nanoparticles.  This composite is a promising anode material for LIBs even though the kinetics of the charge process requires further improvement.  Coaxial electrospinning is a good method for the prepn. of nanomaterials with hollow core/shell architectures.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqIFTnXkuz59rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li6xtynPBPYXw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD1MXhtVWiu7%252FI&amp;md5=a55ca97a6ba2067d924f5763fe8a7b89</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1038/srep02169"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wong, J.                         cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Self-assembly of hierarchical MoSx/CNT nanocomposites (2&lt;x&lt;3): towards high performance anode materials for lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi Yumeng; Wang Ye; Wong Jen It; Tan Alex Yuan Sheng; Hsu Chang-Lung; Li Lain-Jong; Lu Yi-Chun; Yang Hui Ying</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2169</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Two dimension (2D) layered molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) has emerged as a promising candidate for the anode material in lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  Herein, 2D MoSx (2 ≤ x ≤ 3) nanosheet-coated 1D multiwall carbon nanotubes (MWNTs) nanocomposites with hierarchical architecture were synthesized via a high-throughput solvent thermal method under low temperature at 200°C.  The unique hierarchical nanostructures with MWNTs backbone and nanosheets of MoSx have significantly promoted the electrode performance in LIBs.  Every single MoSx nanosheet interconnect to MWNTs centers with maximized exposed electrochemical active sites, which significantly enhance ion diffusion efficiency and accommodate volume expansion during the electrochemical reaction.  A remarkably high specific capacity (i.e., &gt; 1000 mAh/g) was achieved at the current density of 50 mA g(-1), which is much higher than theoretical numbers for either MWNTs or MoS2 along (~372 and ~670 mAh/g, respectively).  We anticipate 2D nanosheets/1D MWNTs nanocomposites will be promising materials in new generation practical LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcT7Oc10qyKIClUIs6wFK5xJfW6udTcc2eYInj9gE-A2p7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3sjptFGqtg%253D%253D&amp;md5=73f987f78ce5f407e8598f18db187a45</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201600116"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.                         cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Situ Carbon-Doped Mo(Se0.85S0.15)2 Hierarchical Nanotubes as Stable Anodes for High-Performance Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Zheng-Tian; Kang, Wenpei; Xu, Jun; Sun, Lian-Ling; Wu, Chunyan; Wang, Li; Yu, Yong-Qiang; Yu, Denis Y. W.; Zhang, Wenjun; Lee, Chun-Sing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Small</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5667-5674</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SMALBC</span>;
