    </div><div class="casAbstract">Two dimension (2D) layered molybdenum disulfide (MoS2) has emerged as a promising candidate for the anode material in lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  Herein, 2D MoSx (2 ≤ x ≤ 3) nanosheet-coated 1D multiwall carbon nanotubes (MWNTs) nanocomposites with hierarchical architecture were synthesized via a high-throughput solvent thermal method under low temperature at 200°C.  The unique hierarchical nanostructures with MWNTs backbone and nanosheets of MoSx have significantly promoted the electrode performance in LIBs.  Every single MoSx nanosheet interconnect to MWNTs centers with maximized exposed electrochemical active sites, which significantly enhance ion diffusion efficiency and accommodate volume expansion during the electrochemical reaction.  A remarkably high specific capacity (i.e., &gt; 1000 mAh/g) was achieved at the current density of 50 mA g(-1), which is much higher than theoretical numbers for either MWNTs or MoS2 along (~372 and ~670 mAh/g, respectively).  We anticipate 2D nanosheets/1D MWNTs nanocomposites will be promising materials in new generation practical LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcT7Oc10qyKIClUIs6wFK5xJfW6udTcc2eZxd_MYk_KseLntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3sjptFGqtg%253D%253D&amp;md5=73f987f78ce5f407e8598f18db187a45</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref54" class="rightTabRefNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit54" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201600116"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are promising energy storage devices, but suffer from poor cycling stability and low rate capability.  In this work, carbon doped Mo(Se0.85S0.15)2 (i.e., Mo(Se0.85S0.15)2:C) hierarchical nanotubes have been synthesized for the first time and serve as a robust and high-performance anode material.  The hierarchical nanotubes with diams. of 300 nm and wall thicknesses of 50 nm consist of numerous 2D layered nanosheets, and can act as a robust host for sodiation/desodiation cycling.  The Mo(Se0.85S0.15)2:C hierarchical nanotubes deliver a discharge capacity of 360 mAh/g at a high c.d. of 2000 mA/g and keep a 81.8% capacity retention compared to that at a c.d. of 50 mA/g, showing superior rate capability.  Comparing with the second cycle discharge capacities, the nanotube anode can maintain capacities of 102.2%, 101.9%, and 97.8% after 100 cycles at current densities of 200, 500, and 1000 mA/g, resp.  This work demonstrates the best cycling performance and high-rate sodium storage capabilities of MoSe2 for SIBs to date.  The hollow interior, hierarchical organization, layered structure, and carbon doping are beneficial for fast Na+-ion and electron kinetics and are responsible for the stable cycling performance and high rate capabilities.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoPfGGClak727Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj87o9Edscbdw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVOmtL3E&amp;md5=97e077a61934425750f57f5f2e0c2e48</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref56" class="rightTabRefNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit56" data-doi="10.1021/nn300098m"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.                         rightTab-cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Oxygen Bridges between NiO Nanosheets and Graphene for Improvement of Lithium Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Guangmin; Wang, Da-Wei; Yin, Li-Chang; Li, Na; Li, Feng; Cheng, Hui-Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors report oxygen bridges between graphene with oxygen functional groups and NiO from anal. by XPS, Fourier transform IR spectroscopy, and Raman spectroscopy, and they also confirm the conformation of oxygen bridges by first-principles calcns.  NiO nanosheets (NiO NSs) are found to be bonded strongly to graphene through oxygen bridges.  The oxygen bridges mainly originate from the pinning of hydroxyl/epoxy groups from graphene on the Ni atoms of NiO NSs.  The calcd. adsorption energies (1.37 and 1.84 eV for graphene with hydroxyl and epoxy) of a Ni adatom on oxygenated graphene by binding with oxygen are comparable with that on graphene (1.26 eV).  However, the calcd. diffusion barriers of the Ni adatom on the oxygenated graphene surface (2.23 and 1.69 eV for graphene with hydroxyl and epoxy) are much larger than that on the graphene (0.19 eV).  Therefore, the NiO NS is anchored strongly on the graphene through a C-O-Ni bridge, which allows a high reversible capacity and excellent rate performance.  The easy binding/difficult dissocg. characteristic of Ni adatoms on the oxygenated graphene facilitates fast electron hopping from graphene to NiO and thus the reversible lithiation and delithiation of NiO.  The understanding of this oxygen bridge between graphene and NiO will lead to the development of other high-performance electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr26TL2YHdDibVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj87o9Edscbdw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XktVGgtrg%253D&amp;md5=eebb442a11e7461631544aff9b18c88c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref57" class="rightTabRefNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit57" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2013.10.022"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Weng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shan, X.                         rightTab-cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Monolithic Fe2O3/graphene hybrid for highly efficient lithium storage and arsenic removal</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Lu; Zhou, Guangmin; Weng, Zhe; Shan, Xu-Yi; Li, Feng; Cheng, Hui-Ming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">We fabricated a monolithic Fe2O3/graphene hybrid directly by hydrothermal reaction of ferrous oxalate dihydrate and graphene oxide without using a reducing agent.  The reduced graphene oxide formed an interconnected network structure that can be used as a support for homogeneous distribution of active Fe2O3 nanoparticles.                         rightTab-cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Origin of non-SEI related coulombic efficiency loss in carbons tested against Na and Li</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Memarzadeh Lotfabad, Elmira; Kalisvaart, Peter; Kohandehghan, Alireza; Karpuzov, Dimitre; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">46</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">19685-19695</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Partially ordered but not graphitized carbons are widely employed for sodium and lithium ion battery (NIB and LIB) anodes, either in their pure form or as a secondary supporting phase for oxides, sulfides and insertion electrodes.  These "pseudographitic" materials ubiquitously display a poor initial coulombic efficiency (CE), which has been historically attributed to solid electrolyte interface (SEI) formation on their large surface areas (up to ∼2500 m2 g-1).  Here we identify the other sources CE loss by examg. a pseudographitic carbon with a state-of-the-art capacity (&gt;350 mA h g-1 for NIB, &gt;800 mA h g-1 for LIB), but with a purposely designed low surface area (14.5 m2 g-1) that disqualifies SEI from having a substantial role.  During the initial several (&lt;5) cycles both Na and Li are irreversibly trapped in the bulk, with the assocd. CE loss occurring at higher desodiation/delithiation voltages.  We measure a progressively increasing graphene interlayer spacing and a progressively increasing Raman G band intensity, indicating that the charge carriers become trapped not only at the graphene defects but also between the graphene planes hence causing them to both dilate and order.  For the case of Li, we also unambiguously detected irreversible metal underpotential deposition ("nanoplating") within the nanopores at roughly below 0.2 V.  It is expected that in conventional high surface area carbons these mechanisms will be a major contributor to CE loss in parallel to classic SEI formation.  Key implications to emerge from these findings are that improvements in early cycling CE may be achieved by synthesizing pseudographitic carbons with lower levels of trapping defects, but that for LIBs the large cycle 1 CE loss may be unavoidable if highly porous structures are utilized.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrS77pE8Yg31rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj87o9Edscbdw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhslGnsrbF&amp;md5=a1179605823e145123e603316b82ac0c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref60"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref60" class="rightTabRefNumLink">60</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit60" data-doi="10.1016/j.nanoen.2016.02.009"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, Z.                         rightTab-cas_cit60R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">60</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical nanotubes assembled from MoS2-carbon monolayer sandwiched superstructure nanosheets for high-performance sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shi, Zheng-Tian; Kang, Wenpei; Xu, Jun; Sun, Yi-Wen; Jiang, Miao; Ng, Tsz-Wai; Xue, Hong-Tao; Yu, Denis Y. W.; Zhang, Wenjun; Lee, Chun-Sing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">22</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">27-37</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NEANCA</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Interface engineering on 2D layered nanomaterials plays pivotal roles in achieving novel properties and superior device performance.  In this work, hierarchical nanotubes consisting of 2D monolayer MoS2 and carbon (MoS2:C) interoverlapped superstructure nanosheets have been synthesized, in which the MoS2 and carbon layers are alternately sandwiched.  The hierarchical architectures assembled from the MoS2:C superstructures are beneficial for: (i) providing substantially expanded (002) interlayer spacing (0.98 nm) of 2H-MoS2 which facilitates fast Na+ insertion/extn. reaction kinetics, (ii) improving elec. cond. of MoS2 by carbon monolayer insertion with ideal heterointerface contact, (iii) preventing aggregation of MoS2 nanosheets, and (iv) accommodating vol. change upon sodiation/desodiation.  The superstructure nanotubes are demonstrated as a robust anode material for sodium storage with superior electrochem. performance.  They deliver a high rate-capability and maintain discharge capacities of 295 and 187 mAh g-1 at high current densities of 10.0 and 20.0 A g-1, resp.  Furthermore, they show durable cycling life (capacity retention of 101.3%, 108.2% and 107.8% after 200 cycles at current densities of 0.2, 0.5 and 1.0 A g-1, resp., in comparison to those of the 2nd cycles), and an initial Coulombic efficiency as high as 84%.  The MoS2:C superstructure nanotubes perform among the best of current MoS2-based electrode materials.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqPqvqO_ClQJ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj87o9Edscbdw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XitlGju7w%253D&amp;md5=250b77306f2bd58ddc6f89017d5b9702</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref61"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref61" class="rightTabRefNumLink">61</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit61" data-doi="10.1126/sciadv.1600021"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y. M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, X. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Paik, U.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lou, X. W. D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical MoS<sub>2</sub> Tubular Structures Internally Wired by Carbon Nanotubes as a Highly Stable Anode Material for Lithium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Sci. Adv.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>2</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">e1600021</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1126/sciadv.1600021</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit61R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">61</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical MoS2 tubular structures internally wired by carbon nanotubes as a highly stable anode material for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Yu Ming; Yu, Xin Yao; Li, Zhen; Paik, Ungyu; Lou, Xiong Wen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">e1600021/1-e1600021/8</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">SACDAF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2375-2548</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Association for the Advancement of Science</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Molybdenum disulfide (MoS2), a typical two-dimensional material, is a promising anode material for lithium-ion batteries because it has three times the theor. capacity of graphite.  The main challenges assocd. with MoS2 anodes are the structural degrdn. and the low rate capability caused by the low intrinsic elec. cond. and large strain upon cycling.  Here, we design hierarchical MoS2 tubular structures internally wired by carbon nanotubes (CNTs) to tackle these problems.  These porous MoS2 tubular structures are constructed from building blocks of ultrathin nanosheets, which are believed to benefit the electrochem. reactions.  Benefiting from the unique structural and compositional characteristics, these CNT-wired MoS2 tubular structures deliver a very high specific capacity of ∼1320 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 0.1 A g-1, exceptional rate capability, and an ultralong cycle life of up to 1000 cycles.  This work may inspire new ideas for constructing high-performance electrodes for electrochem. energy storage.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqLqG3NcsZpD7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj87o9Edscbdw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXkslKqtrY%253D&amp;md5=3822cd8ff4ff4d1425ce9ffab4e30a04</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref62"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref62" class="rightTabRefNumLink">62</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit62" data-doi="10.1021/jp5080847"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">David, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Singh, G.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Reduced Graphene Oxide Paper Electrode: Opposing Effect of Thermal Annealing on Li and Na Cyclability</span>. <i>J. Phys. Chem. C</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>118</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">28401</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">28408</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jp5080847</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit62R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">62</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reduced graphene oxide paper electrode: opposing effect of thermal annealing on Li and Na cyclability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">David, Lamuel; Singh, Gurpreet</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">118</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">49</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">28401-28408</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">We study long-term electrochem. sodium and lithium cycling, and tensile testing behavior of thermally reduced graphene oxide (rGO) paper electrodes.  We find strong dependence of annealing temp. and gas environment on the elec. cond., electrochem. capacity, and rate capability of the electrodes.  The effect, however, was opposing for the two cell types.  Lithium charge capacity increased with increasing annealing temps. reaching a stable value of ∼325 mAh·ganode-1 (∼100 mAh·cm-3anode at ∼48 μA·cm-2 with respect to total vol. of the electrode) for specimen annealed at 900 °C, while a sharp decline in Na charge capacity was noted for rGO annealed above 500 °C.  Maximum sodium charge capacity of ∼140 mAh·g-1anode at 100 mA·g-1anode (∼98 mAh·cmanode-3 at ∼70 μA·cm-2) was realized for specimen reduced at 500 °C.  These values are the highest reported for GO paper electrodes.  More important, annealing of GO in NH3 environment resulted in a complete shutdown of its Na-ion cyclability showing near-zero charge capacity.  On the contrary, NH3 annealing only improved the electrode's Li-ion cycling efficiency and rate capability.  This behavior is attributed to the increased level of ordering in graphene sheets and decreased interlayer spacing with increasing annealing temps. in Ar or redn. at moderate temps. in NH3 atmosphere.  Further, uniaxial tensile tests and videog. highlighted the superior elasticity and high strain to failure of crumpled paper electrodes.  The present work provides new insights toward the optimization and design of Li and other larger metal-ion battery electrodes where graphene is utilized as an active material, conductive agent, or a flexible mech. support.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoGdOAwV_WOSbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljWmbtvLFnMwQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFGgu7jE&amp;md5=0b8e62bfe498e00c94c41af986475296</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref63"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref63" class="rightTabRefNumLink">63</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit63" data-doi="10.1016/j.mtener.2018.04.001"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zeng, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">von Bülow, J. F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bao, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Graphene Layer Reinforcing Mesoporous Molybdenum Disulfide Foam as High-Performance Anode for Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Mater. Today Energy</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">151</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">156</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.mtener.2018.04.001</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R

Funct. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>27</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1604941</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adfm.201604941</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="

		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();

})();

<script nonce="90da8f98ffc7b325-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

)|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>

var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
